  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_c63f16d2-fc51-4642-a3ea-0625a747393d'
      });
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer573545081479187084">Eva Nine is a curious and sensitive twelve-year-old who has existed only in a subterranean home called Sanctuary, cared for by a robot named Muthr. Eva's great desire is to go aboveground, and her wish comes true, though not as she had imagined. On the surface, Eva goes in search of other humans--she has never met one--and soon meets both friend and foe.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17259646472643325985">4.5 <br/><br/>Lovely and wonderful! </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_759926938" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/759926938" />
    <a title="Rick Riordan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25375513-rick-riordan"><img alt="Rick Riordan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442449448p2/25375513.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/759926938?book_show_action=true">Nov 08, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rick Riordan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rick Riordan" href="/user/show/25375513-rick-riordan">Rick Riordan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer759926938" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13479434662004692526">This book makes me wish I could draw. From the co-creator of Spiderwick Chronicles, The Search for Wondla is a fabulous cross between sci fi and fantasy. A young girl, raised in an underground bunker by a motherly robot, is suddenly forced to the surface and finds that the world is radically changed -- if it's even the planet she thought it was. The story is fascinating by itself, but the illustrations add a whole new dimension to the adventure. Highly recommended.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1787239934" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1787239934" />
    <a title="Melanie (TBR and Beyond)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47129377-melanie-tbr-and-beyond"><img alt="Melanie (TBR and Beyond)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1494279381p2/47129377.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1787239934?book_show_action=true">Mar 17, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie (TBR and Beyond)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie (TBR and Beyond)" href="/user/show/47129377-melanie-tbr-and-beyond">Melanie (TBR and Beyond)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47129377-melanie-tbr-and-beyond?shelf=ya-fantasy">ya-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47129377-melanie-tbr-and-beyond?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47129377-melanie-tbr-and-beyond?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47129377-melanie-tbr-and-beyond?shelf=underrated-gem">underrated-gem</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47129377-melanie-tbr-and-beyond?shelf=ya-science-fiction">ya-science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47129377-melanie-tbr-and-beyond?shelf=illustrations">illustrations</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47129377-melanie-tbr-and-beyond?shelf=cry-worthy">cry-worthy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47129377-melanie-tbr-and-beyond?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47129377-melanie-tbr-and-beyond?shelf=top-2017-reads">top-2017-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1787239934" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4278760399840606414"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“Welcome to the real world, Mother Robot, a beautiful and dangerous place. Now you can truly begin to live.” </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>You can find this review and all of my other reviews at <a href='http://www.noveldescent.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>Novel Descent</a> Thanks for the support!<br/><br/>I was completely engrossed in this book from the start. The characters, the world, the illustrations - all had me wanting to know and explore more. <br/><br/><i>The Search for Wondla</i> is about a young human girl, Eva Nine, who is 12 years old and has been brought up in an underground sanctuary by he</span>
  <span id="freeText4278760399840606414" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“Welcome to the real world, Mother Robot, a beautiful and dangerous place. Now you can truly begin to live.” </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />You can find this review and all of my other reviews at <a href="http://www.noveldescent.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Novel Descent</a> Thanks for the support!<br /><br />I was completely engrossed in this book from the start. The characters, the world, the illustrations - all had me wanting to know and explore more. <br /><br /><i>The Search for Wondla</i> is about a young human girl, Eva Nine, who is 12 years old and has been brought up in an underground sanctuary by her robot mother. She has never seen another human and knows nothing of the outside world and its beauty and dangers. Eva Nine's house goes under siege by a a large monster-like hunter and everything she knows is destroyed. She must make her way in a new world and find where she came from and maybe make some interesting friends along the way. <br /><br />I just loved this book. The first book is all about world-building and discovering this strange and mysterious land. Everything is new and dangerous. This book felt like Wizard of Oz meets Star Wars. My little fan girl heart was pretty pumped from the start really. This book is mainly a fantasy and adventure story mixed in with a few science-fiction elements. The genres mesh really well together and the the story was a fast quick read. <br /><br />I think the strongest element this book has going for it is the detail to the world building. You feel like you are discovering everything right along with Eva Nine. You can feel the wonderment and fear as she's figuring it out herself. I was 100% along for the journey with her. I loved Otto, the water bear - he was so sweet. I wouldn't say he was deep character with all kinds of layers to discover but it was kind of nice that he was simple and safe. Another character we meet is named Rovee, he really wasn't fleshed out at all till the end so he kind of seems to just be there for awhile to play the grumpy side character. By the end though, I felt like I knew him and his motivations and he became much more three dimensional for me overall. I think in the next book we will really see this character develop. Muther, the robot, was a pretty interesting character. I loved the idea of a robot trying to work through emotions and information, despite what her programming was telling them. I wish they would've taken her storyline a little further, there was a ton of potential there. I know the book was already almost 500 pages, but I really think she could've used some more fleshing out. Eva Nine was a relatable and likable protagonist. I think most people will enjoy her character and she still has lots of room for growth. The villain of the story was a hunter named Beestal, he was alright. I thought he was going to be really scary because when we first meet him, he really seems to have no conscience. I found him to be a little one-dimensional in the end though and pretty much everyone else in the story interested me more. <br /><br />I can't talk about this book without talking about Tony DiTerrlizzi's beautiful illustrations. They are through-out the book and they add such a wonderful element to the reading experience. You get to look at the author's creations through their eyes and I was very happy for it. I wish more books would do this. <br /><br />This book was't flawless but I'm rating it five stars on pure enjoyment. I will be finishing the series. This book is very family friendly - would be a great book to read to any child probably about eight and over. I highly recommend this book and this is one where it really is worth the price of a hardcover - just for how nice it looks with the illustrations.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4278760399840606414" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17545683723816911963">Oh. My. God. I don't even have the words to describe this WondLa-ful book! This book is steeped in emotion of being alone in the world, adventure, and friendship. This is like a soup, its ingredients include; a teaspoon of The Wizard of Oz, a drop of Treasure Planet, and a dash of Avatar (with the whole nature thing, and of course Rovee being a blue creature). Oh, and a bit of Journey to the Center of the Earth for good measure.<br/><br/>The plot is completely original, well done to Tony's imagination! An</span>
  <span id="freeText17545683723816911963" style="display:none">Oh. My. God. I don't even have the words to describe this WondLa-ful book! This book is steeped in emotion of being alone in the world, adventure, and friendship. This is like a soup, its ingredients include; a teaspoon of The Wizard of Oz, a drop of Treasure Planet, and a dash of Avatar (with the whole nature thing, and of course Rovee being a blue creature). Oh, and a bit of Journey to the Center of the Earth for good measure.<br /><br />The plot is completely original, well done to Tony's imagination! And well done to his writing, too! For it was simply divine.<br /><br />Eva Nine is such a relatable character, she is brave, strong willed, and understandably lonely. Muther was so sweet. All she wanted to do was protect Eva from the outside world she did not understand! Otto; HE'S SO CUTE!!!!!! Rovender is friendly and treats both Eva and Muther nicely - but he can be a little jumpy. I haven't made my mind on him. Maybe I'll make up my mind on the next book...<br /><br />Speaking of the next book, you'll want to read it straight after The Search For WondLa. Because: Cliff-Hanger alert! Ooo and what a cliff-hanger it is. </span>

<div id="review_156435099" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/156435099" />
    <a title="Vicky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4896571-vicky"><img alt="Vicky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1558522226p2/4896571.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/156435099?book_show_action=true">Mar 24, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vicky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vicky" href="/user/show/4896571-vicky">Vicky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer156435099" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7960354302343173571">Take a little bit of “The Wizard of Oz” and “Alice in Wonderland”, toss in some “Star Wars” and “Planet of the Apes”, mix well by a talented writer and you’ll have an idea of this book. From the fantastic mind of Tony DiTerlizzi, creator of the Spiderwick Chronicles, this is the first of a three part series.<br/><br/>The story concerns a twelve-year-old girl, Eva Nine, who has been raised in an underground sanctuary by a robot named Muthr. When a vicious hunter destroys the sanctuary in search of Eva, she</span>
  <span id="freeText7960354302343173571" style="display:none">Take a little bit of “The Wizard of Oz” and “Alice in Wonderland”, toss in some “Star Wars” and “Planet of the Apes”, mix well by a talented writer and you’ll have an idea of this book. From the fantastic mind of Tony DiTerlizzi, creator of the Spiderwick Chronicles, this is the first of a three part series.<br /><br />The story concerns a twelve-year-old girl, Eva Nine, who has been raised in an underground sanctuary by a robot named Muthr. When a vicious hunter destroys the sanctuary in search of Eva, she is forced to go above ground for the first tie in her life. Up there, she finds odd creatures, but no one like her. She sets off across the land to find other humans. With the help of kind, though strange, friends, she runs for her life from the hunter and heads for the badlands where it is rumored she may find other humans.<br /><br />Mr. DiTerlizzi is a master craftsman with this genre. His characterizations, world building, and settings are so well done, you believe there may actually be a world like this one. The story flows well and is enjoyable from page one to the last chapter. According to the information accompanying this pre-pub copy, there will also be an interactive web site so readers can journey along with Eva and her friends, just the sort of thing any young tween would like.<br /><br />If there are any drawbacks at all for me, it is that the last page leaves you dangling. This is definitely not a stand alone book and it will be necessary to get the other books to finish the story, a marketing ploy that continually frustrates me. But other than this minor, and not unexpected, issue, I highly recommend The Search for WondLa. I am definitely looking forward to the others<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7960354302343173571" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer379220713" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer11301808546026323057">I would have liked more consistency throughout this story. I think the concept is wonderful, though perhaps a bit reminiscent of "Planet of the Apes", and the environment is imaginative and fun. It would be a fantastic romp for 8-13 year-olds.<br/>Personally, however, I was disappointed by the shifting nature of both Eva Nine's and MUTHR's characters and not in a way that showed they were growing and becoming new people. Rather, I felt they had multiple personalities and I never knew which one I'd be</span>
  <span id="freeText11301808546026323057" style="display:none">I would have liked more consistency throughout this story. I think the concept is wonderful, though perhaps a bit reminiscent of "Planet of the Apes", and the environment is imaginative and fun. It would be a fantastic romp for 8-13 year-olds.<br />Personally, however, I was disappointed by the shifting nature of both Eva Nine's and MUTHR's characters and not in a way that showed they were growing and becoming new people. Rather, I felt they had multiple personalities and I never knew which one I'd be dealing with from chapter to chapter. I had a hard time warming up to either of these characters because I couldn't trust them to be themselves.<br />The one character who never broke stride was Besteel and that was just as irritating as Eva and MUTHR changing their behavior every few chapters. He was a bit of overkill.<br />I think with some more tweaking, some snipping and cutting and some rearranging, this could be an amazing story. For me, however, it was not.<br />I don't think any of that will get in the way of a young reader's enjoyment of this story, however. Plus, the illustrations are, per usual, phenomenal and they definitely add another level of interest.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14882919202289707318">Let me begin by encouraging anyone who is thinking about downloading the e-book edition of this story to go out and buy the real thing. In <u>hardback</u>. Trust me, it's worth it. A book this beautiful is meant to be printed and bound for art-enthusiasts and sci-fi/fantasy nerds everywhere to drool over.<br/><br/>Secondly, I'd like to congratulate DiTerlizzi on producing such a brilliant, original children's story. Not only is each chapter of this book beautifully illustrated by the author, the story itself suc</span>
  <span id="freeText14882919202289707318" style="display:none">Let me begin by encouraging anyone who is thinking about downloading the e-book edition of this story to go out and buy the real thing. In <u>hardback</u>. Trust me, it's worth it. A book this beautiful is meant to be printed and bound for art-enthusiasts and sci-fi/fantasy nerds everywhere to drool over.<br /><br />Secondly, I'd like to congratulate DiTerlizzi on producing such a brilliant, original children's story. Not only is each chapter of this book beautifully illustrated by the author, the story itself sucked me in from the very first page, and DiTerlizzi's whimsical descriptions were as rich and vivid as the illustrations themselves. Though I still love children's fiction, it's rare nowadays that a story aimed at pre-teens can demand my attention in the way that classics such as <i>Charlotte Sometimes</i> and <i>Harry Potter and the Philosopher's Stone</i> once could. Reading <i>The Search for WondLa</i>, I felt myself escaping into the world of Orbona the way I used to with my favourite childhood reads. As a huge fan of his work on <i>The Spiderwick Chronicles</i> with Holly Black, I wouldn't have thought it was possible, but DiTerlizzi has exceeded my expectations. I only wish I had half his imagination and creativity.<br /><br />I recommend this story to any reader aged seven and up (including adults who, like me, find it impossible to stop reading books marketed at kids). <i>The Search for WondLa</i> has all the components of a new children's classic in the making, and I look forward to seeing what more DiTerlizzi has to offer from this enchanting new world.<br /><br /><b>Title:</b> The Search for WondLa<br /><b>Author:</b> Tony DiTerlizzi<br /><b>Rating:</b> 5 stars<br /></span>

          </span>

<div id="review_348828613" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/348828613" />
    <a title="C.S. Einfeld" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7070022-c-s-einfeld"><img alt="C.S. Einfeld" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442612005p2/7070022.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/348828613?book_show_action=true">Jun 15, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.S. Einfeld" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.S. Einfeld" href="/user/show/7070022-c-s-einfeld">C.S. Einfeld</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer348828613" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1782851746872851703">WondLa = Wonderful? <br/><br/>Meh, not so much. <br/><br/>I had a really hard time rating this book about Eva Nine, possibly the last human girl alive in an alien world. <br/> <br/>There were a lot of things I really enjoyed about The Search For WondLa by Tony DiTerlizzi: the main character, Eva, is very engaging, as is her "Muther" robot and many of the creatures she meets on her quest to find other humans and to escape the evil huntsman, Beesteel. <br/><br/>The story started as strong as any I've ever read. I recall--explicitly--say</span>
  <span id="freeText1782851746872851703" style="display:none">WondLa = Wonderful? <br /><br />Meh, not so much. <br /><br />I had a really hard time rating this book about Eva Nine, possibly the last human girl alive in an alien world. <br /> <br />There were a lot of things I really enjoyed about The Search For WondLa by Tony DiTerlizzi: the main character, Eva, is very engaging, as is her "Muther" robot and many of the creatures she meets on her quest to find other humans and to escape the evil huntsman, Beesteel. <br /><br />The story started as strong as any I've ever read. I recall--explicitly--saying out-loud, "Oh, yay! It's going to be good!" after reading the first chapter. Even through the first hundred pages of character introduction and world building, I was seriously feeling the five stars. <br /><br />And then, the "middle". <br /><br />YAWN. <br /><br />Two hundred pages of repetitive world-building. I found myself asking, "Okay...is something, ANYTHING significant going to happen any time soon? <br /><br />And then, when the odd thing did, it was over so fast and so anti-climactic (Oh, look! She escaped Beesteel, again....), that frankly, I started getting annoyed. <br /><br />Fortunately, I kept at it and was rewarded with a satisfactory ending. Over-all, though, I feel this book held such great promise but for me, was cumulatively underwhelming. <br /><br />I give the first 100 pages five stars, the next 200 pages, 2 stars, and the final 100 pages, 4 stars. Add to that a hearty five stars for the illustrations (I loved those--all of them), and we eek out a weak 3 stars on the whole. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1782851746872851703" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_826733157" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/826733157" />
    <a title="Kendra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1743444-kendra"><img alt="Kendra" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1310355595p2/1743444.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/826733157?book_show_action=true">Jan 17, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kendra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kendra" href="/user/show/1743444-kendra">Kendra</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1743444-kendra?shelf=children-s-books">children-s-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1743444-kendra?shelf=sci-fi-fantasy">sci-fi-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1743444-kendra?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer826733157" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13034383624766806507">***may contain a minor spoiler without revealing any plot information***<br/>My 8 year old and I really enjoyed reading this book together...it combined the elements of science fiction that I like; being plunked down in a completely different realm and trying to figure it out with the character, some clues and connection to biology and astronomy. This is good dystopian fiction for those who may find the genre dark, or for younger kids who might be interested in the genre but not ready for the YA/Adul</span>
  <span id="freeText13034383624766806507" style="display:none">***may contain a minor spoiler without revealing any plot information***<br />My 8 year old and I really enjoyed reading this book together...it combined the elements of science fiction that I like; being plunked down in a completely different realm and trying to figure it out with the character, some clues and connection to biology and astronomy. This is good dystopian fiction for those who may find the genre dark, or for younger kids who might be interested in the genre but not ready for the YA/Adult themes that are found in most of the texts on the subject - there is one somewhat graphic description of the butchery of a "water bear"...it is within context and sets up the characterization of the main "villain", and it is not gratuitous, but it may be a little unsettling for those under 8 or 9 (or even older); even my son and I took pause and talked about the scene and how the other characters reacted. Some reviewers complained that the plot was predictable and/or that the language was repetitive; I think for the intended audience that this holds a lot of suspense and has lots of "aha" moments, and I didn't find too many repetitive elements. In order to read this book aloud, the reader has to get used to the author's style of joining dialog to the action of the speaker, but this is minor. If anything, I didn't care for the "prophesy" part of it, but it was such a minor part of it that it didn't really distract. WE are on to book two with great enthusiasm!<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13034383624766806507" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a title="Madeline O&#39;Rourke" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Madeline O&#39;Rourke" href="/user/show/64752900-madeline-o-rourke">Madeline O&#39;Rourke</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781471104947" href="/book/show/16172049-the-search-for-wondla">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64752900-madeline-o-rourke?shelf=library-reads">library-reads</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2580651542" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5126303927848236385">There's so much I objectively love about <i>The Search for WondLa</i>, but it didn't quite grab me—I'll definitely be continuing with the series, though!<br/><br/>Set in a mystery world and accompanied by gorgeous illustrations, I loved a lot of things about the construction of the novel. I loved that one of the three main characters is a robot mother, but one with emotions, who cares a whole lot about her human 'assignment'. I loved the depiction of Eva Nine, and thought that her twelve-year-old emotions were d</span>
  <span id="freeText5126303927848236385" style="display:none">There's so much I objectively love about <i>The Search for WondLa</i>, but it didn't quite grab me—I'll definitely be continuing with the series, though!<br /><br />Set in a mystery world and accompanied by gorgeous illustrations, I loved a lot of things about the construction of the novel. I loved that one of the three main characters is a robot mother, but one with emotions, who cares a whole lot about her human 'assignment'. I loved the depiction of Eva Nine, and thought that her twelve-year-old emotions were done really well. I loved the role of technology, the small hints about where and when the story is set, and the many creatures that populate the world. The story includes light-hearted moments and moments of loss, there's no romance, and it's got a dynamic main trio who I really enjoyed reading about.<br /><br />This is a strong middle grade fantasy novel. It may not have quite captivated me, but it certainly did more than enough for me to want to continue the series. Like many trilogies, the story is set to radically expand in the second instalment, and I'm excited to see where it leads, because there are still so many questions unanswered about this world.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1702005084" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1702005084" />
    <a title="Milou" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8585586-milou"><img alt="Milou" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483917670p2/8585586.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1702005084?book_show_action=true">May 16, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Milou" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Milou" href="/user/show/8585586-milou">Milou</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8585586-milou?shelf=2020">2020</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1702005084" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5288442451969924984">I really enjoyed this book. I feel there isn't that much middle-grade scifi... and I don't get why because this book shows it can be great!<br/><br/>Like for example The Hobbit, this never read like a kids book to me. It was just a great book, in which we happen to follow 12 year old Eva. She has lived in the Sanctuary her whole life, training survival skills with her caretaker robot. When their home gets attacked Eva is forced to go above ground... only to find out she isn't on Earth and her survival ski</span>
  <span id="freeText5288442451969924984" style="display:none">I really enjoyed this book. I feel there isn't that much middle-grade scifi... and I don't get why because this book shows it can be great!<br /><br />Like for example The Hobbit, this never read like a kids book to me. It was just a great book, in which we happen to follow 12 year old Eva. She has lived in the Sanctuary her whole life, training survival skills with her caretaker robot. When their home gets attacked Eva is forced to go above ground... only to find out she isn't on Earth and her survival skills aren't all that useful after all . Together with her robot mother, a giant water bear, and grumpy alien Rovee she travels through this new world to find other humans, whilst constantly being hunted down.<br /><br />First of, this book has some beautiful illustrations (although not all very strategically placed and therefore slightly spoiling the story at times). They are very simple in colour scheme, but that doesn't make them any less stunning. <br /><br /> <br /><br /> <br /><br />The world building is just great. Some of my favourite parts are just Eva exploring and studying the plants and animals around her. I also really liked all of the characters. Otto is the sweetest, and his communication with Eva is very clever. Something I hope is explored more in the sequels. Rovee is only really fleshed out by the end of the book, yet his bickering and banter with mother robot is a joy to read. Eva is just a normal, relatable, girl... and I love her. The prophecy regarding her was interesting enough, but it didn't add anything to the story so far. That and the fact that this book felt a bit too long are the only elements keeping this from a perfect read for me. Oh, and I didn't really understand the ending... but I'm sure it'll become clear in the sequel. Which I am very excited for!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5288442451969924984" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14766077580473227305">This book was certainly full of wonder and adventure. The characters under went quite the experience on a very daring trip full of curious and dangerous creatures in a completely new world. Or at least one unknown to us and our main character Eva.<br/>Many questions arose for me while reading this book, and I know they will be answered soon, and that makes me even more excited to see where this story goes.<br/>I loved the characters and how they grew to know each other and rely on one another.   <span id="freeText14766077580473227305" style="display:none">This book was certainly full of wonder and adventure. The characters under went quite the experience on a very daring trip full of curious and dangerous creatures in a completely new world. Or at least one unknown to us and our main character Eva.<br />Many questions arose for me while reading this book, and I know they will be answered soon, and that makes me even more excited to see where this story goes.<br />I loved the characters and how they grew to know each other and rely on one another. I loved how Eva grew, going from a secluded young girl who couldn’t pass a simulation to being suddenly thrust upon a world totally new to her and not at all like what she thought it was supposed to be. Muthr certainly did act like a mother figure, helping to guide our characters along the way in this journey and keep them on the right path. <br />It was a very entertaining story, and the only thing left to do, is see where this adventure takes us.<br />3.5/5 stars</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1574195939131214878">I just don't get it.....<br/>I really wanted to love this book and it gets such amazing reviews from literally everyone, but I didn't connect with this story at all.<br/>Part of my problem was that I found Eva's reactions and behavior completely unbelievable.   <span id="freeText1574195939131214878" style="display:none">I just don't get it.....<br />I really wanted to love this book and it gets such amazing reviews from literally everyone, but I didn't connect with this story at all.<br />Part of my problem was that I found Eva's reactions and behavior completely unbelievable. If she had been raised by robots in a bunker, she would not a) talk and act so human, and b) she would not be so relaxed about leaving the bunker which has been her entire world her whole life!<br />There were such deep psychological issues that could have been explored pertaining to how she was raised and how that would make her see the world, but they were just glossed over to make room for alien-laser-gun-fighting-action. <br />Am I missing something?</span>

  <span id="freeText5862150674355585598" style="display:none">This book was such a pleasant surprise. The story reads like the old Oz stories with the writing styles simplicity. The story doesn't try to be too much all at once, but eases you into the world that DiTerlizzi is creating through the changing worldview of Eva Nine. Often I can only read roughly 50 pages at a time of any book, regardless of genre, but I found myself devouring larger chunks in one sitting because I would lose track of time. The ability to lose yourself in a story is a good benchmark to me if a story is good and this one is. I definitely want to get my hands on the next book!</span>

<div id="review_206269599" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/206269599" />
    <a title="Vincent Desjardins" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3177878-vincent-desjardins"><img alt="Vincent Desjardins" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1266420505p2/3177878.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/206269599?book_show_action=true">Sep 07, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vincent Desjardins" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vincent Desjardins" href="/user/show/3177878-vincent-desjardins">Vincent Desjardins</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3177878-vincent-desjardins?shelf=children-s-and-young-adult">children-s-and-young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3177878-vincent-desjardins?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer206269599&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer206269599" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1982464635612400570">Publicity for this book calls it a fairy tale for the 21st century and DiTerlizzi has said he was inspired by the stories of James M. Barrie and L. Frank Baum. I can see a lot of Baum’s influence in this story of a young girl named Eva Nine who has to make her way through a strange new world to find what she is searching for, in this case the secret behind ‘WondLa,’ a damaged panel she has found containing lettering that appears to spell out the word ‘WondLa.’ The panel also contains an image of</span>
  <span id="freeText1982464635612400570" style="display:none">Publicity for this book calls it a fairy tale for the 21st century and DiTerlizzi has said he was inspired by the stories of James M. Barrie and L. Frank Baum. I can see a lot of Baum’s influence in this story of a young girl named Eva Nine who has to make her way through a strange new world to find what she is searching for, in this case the secret behind ‘WondLa,’ a damaged panel she has found containing lettering that appears to spell out the word ‘WondLa.’ The panel also contains an image of a human girl and what appears to be an adult figure and a robot, all holding hands. Since Eva has grown up in solitude, the only human in an underground sanctuary, watched over by a robot named Muthr, she is intrigued to see this image showing other humans with a robot companion. She begins to wonder if there are others like herself in the world outside her sanctuary, a place she has been forbidden to explore. When Eva Nine’s sanctuary is attacked by a bounty hunter from the outside world, everything Eva thought she knew about the outside world is turned upside down. She and Muthr are forced to flee and end up on a journey in search of WondLa, hoping to find other humans. Along the way they gain friends and encounter enemies. There are some obvious parallels to Dorothy’s trip across the land of Oz. Like Dorothy, Eva Nine has three companions on her journey and also, like Dorothy, she has an enemy on her tail. Though it’s been compared to a fairy tale, the story is told with the trappings of a science fiction adventure. What it does share with many fairy tales is the premise of someone who leaves the safety of their own world and is thrust into a strange world filled with incredible encounters. Eva Nine is a very sympathetic and likable character as are all of her companions. I found the story imaginative, suspenseful and at times very moving. As an added bonus, the talented DiTerlizzi has created some wonderful illustrations for the book. He’s an amazing artist and his illustrations add another dimension to the reading experience. I found myself constantly going back to study the illustrations after reading the corresponding passages in the text. DiTerlizzi has come up with a clever solution for the secret behind the 'WondLa' panel, which I pretty much guessed before the end of the book, but that didn’t spoil it for me (If you’ve seen a cheesy Sean Connery film of the 1970s called ‘Zardoz,’ you might also guess the secret). The book is a fun read and I’m already looking forward to the next installment in this planned trilogy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1982464635612400570" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1539620010" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1539620010" />
    <a title="Dana Salman" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2246621-dana-salman"><img alt="Dana Salman" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1454265334p2/2246621.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1539620010?book_show_action=true">Feb 06, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dana Salman" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dana Salman" href="/user/show/2246621-dana-salman">Dana Salman</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781416983118" href="/book/show/12156463-the-search-for-wondla">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2246621-dana-salman?shelf=boring-books">boring-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2246621-dana-salman?shelf=regret-buying">regret-buying</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2246621-dana-salman?shelf=on-my-bookshelf">on-my-bookshelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2246621-dana-salman?shelf=series-debut">series-debut</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2246621-dana-salman?shelf=seriesitriedandfailedtogetinto">seriesitriedandfailedtogetinto</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2246621-dana-salman?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1539620010" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7159619526767438342">Man, no way was I gonna let this book sit indefinitely on my currently-reading shelf next to <i>The Talisman</i> and Sherlock Holmes - it sure looked like that for awhile though. Exams kept me book-deprived for over two weeks and then the past week I've been preoccupied with getting myself in Ramadan mode.<br/><br/>But like I said in my updates, I didn't really have much of an incentive to continue reading this book other than to just <i>finish</i> it, because this book was just kinda... meh.<br/><br/>I mean don't get me wrong, </span>
  <span id="freeText7159619526767438342" style="display:none">Man, no way was I gonna let this book sit indefinitely on my currently-reading shelf next to <i>The Talisman</i> and Sherlock Holmes - it sure looked like that for awhile though. Exams kept me book-deprived for over two weeks and then the past week I've been preoccupied with getting myself in Ramadan mode.<br /><br />But like I said in my updates, I didn't really have much of an incentive to continue reading this book other than to just <i>finish</i> it, because this book was just kinda... meh.<br /><br />I mean don't get me wrong, I thought all the gadgets Eva uses were creative, and the illustrations were great, and I loved the relationship between Rovendor (probably my favorite character, but that's not really setting the bar that high...) and Eva. But I mean other than all that, I just didn't feel invested or attached to this adventure or these characters at all. Even though it's been more than a year now (I believe) since I finished <i>The Knife of Never Letting Go</i>, I'm still kinda feeling the aftereffects of that book series (given that the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1490181407" rel="nofollow noopener">series I read</a> in between that and <i>WondLa</i> left me with absolutely nothing worth reminiscing about). And the thing I didn't really like about TKoNLG was how it was basically just this long account of two characters running away from someone pursuing them.<br /><br />This book was pretty much like that - just a long journey through different locations, meeting different characters, all while trying to escape the nasty clutches of some relentless pursuer. And I found it boring. Eva wasn't really a strong enough character for me to feel attached to, and neither were any of the creatures she met along the way on her journey. Not even the environment was all that engaging, and in a story all about travelling through unfamiliar lands, environment should have picked up the slack left by the characters. I'm not dumping on the world the author has built up, especially considering the pretty decent plot twist concerning it in the last bit... But it takes a lot more for a story to get me excited than just a long journey riddled with your token monsters and creature companions, and your token allies and enemies. If there had been anything even a bit... well, different, to add some <i>spice</i> to things, I would've been perfectly fine with an exclusively journey-driven story, but everything about this book just felt very by-the-numbers, at least as far as a middle-grade book goes.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7159619526767438342" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_425916423" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/425916423" />
    <a title="Reader the Fish" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7815768-reader-the-fish"><img alt="Reader the Fish" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1361174743p2/7815768.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/425916423?book_show_action=true">Oct 01, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Reader the Fish" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Reader the Fish" href="/user/show/7815768-reader-the-fish">Reader the Fish</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer425916423" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17886978335527012647">What if you learned that you are the only human living in the world? Your mother is a robot, and you've never left your peaceful sanctuary, and never seen the sun before. Until some unknown creature invades you house and you need to escape? Well, this is exactly what happened to Eva Nine, and her Muthur. Eva and her Muthur must escape from the invader, Besteel to kidnap her and take her somewhere. Escaping her sanctuary, there she meets a blue, indigo eyed creature with cat-fish-like whiskers. H</span>
  <span id="freeText17886978335527012647" style="display:none">What if you learned that you are the only human living in the world? Your mother is a robot, and you've never left your peaceful sanctuary, and never seen the sun before. Until some unknown creature invades you house and you need to escape? Well, this is exactly what happened to Eva Nine, and her Muthur. Eva and her Muthur must escape from the invader, Besteel to kidnap her and take her somewhere. Escaping her sanctuary, there she meets a blue, indigo eyed creature with cat-fish-like whiskers. His name is Rovender Kitt, also-known-as Rovee or Mr. Kitt. He helps Eva and her mother escape, but they don't know where to go, but Eva does. She finds a picture of a girl, a robot, and another human together, looking happy, with the caption saying Wondla. There, the trio goes into an epic adventure, meeting other alien species, and organisms. She learns that she's been living underground all her life, and discovers another world above it, with cities like Solas ruled by a royal queen. Finding Wondla is not easy. Hiding from enemies, getting help from allies and friendship, survival skills are things that won't take a day to accomplish, but the brave hearted, kind, and sweet Eva does. Eva is an amazing brave young girl. She has become one of my top five role model since I picked up the book. The story is beautifully described, and I did not regret buying this in hardcover, because my parents aren't the biggest fans for buying hardcover books. It tells a story about survival, friendship, mother-daughter relationships, sacrifice, love, death, kindness, and bravery. It was hard to put this book down. Tony DiTerlizzi is an amazing writer, and has inspired me. The setting he describes in the story makes it so visual, and not just because of the beautiful pictures the author also drew. I fell in love with this book, and I need to get the second book like... NOW!!!!! I loved this book, and is one of my favorite! I would recommend this to kids I see everywhere and even adults. I also believe this book should be a school reading book. It made me cry, laugh, and smile most of all the book. Thank you Mr. DiTerlizzi for writing this book. The Search for Wondla made me felt positive, and I can put my negativity away form me, and I could be braver, and learn more about kindness and friendships.<br /> <br />I might recommend this book to my mother as well.<br /></span>

<div id="review_430771141" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/430771141" />
    <a title="Magenta  Cooly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5461965-magenta-cooly"><img alt="Magenta  Cooly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1318833569p2/5461965.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer430771141" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer5562770694036432214">Wow! Who knew Tony DeTerlizzi could pull off a sci-fi...!<br/>It looked interesting enough sitting on a shelf at Barnes & Noble, but I don't read sci-fi; definitely not my main genre of interest. However, the illustrations are beautiful enough to make anyone want to read it.<br/>Man, I am so glad I did. I almost stopped and left it in the middle, but the adventure the characters are experiencing keeps the fascination up, and the writing, though fairly simple, doesn't lag. The characters in general are a l</span>
  <span id="freeText5562770694036432214" style="display:none">Wow! Who knew Tony DeTerlizzi could pull off a sci-fi...!<br />It looked interesting enough sitting on a shelf at Barnes &amp; Noble, but I don't read sci-fi; definitely not my main genre of interest. However, the illustrations are beautiful enough to make anyone want to read it.<br />Man, I am so glad I did. I almost stopped and left it in the middle, but the adventure the characters are experiencing keeps the fascination up, and the writing, though fairly simple, doesn't lag. The characters in general are a little flat, in the sense that we don't really connect with them, or their emotions very quickly. But the jack-in-the-box in this 484 page journey is a surprisingly tragic moment of greif. If the characters are hard to understand throughout the majority of the book, they certainly make up for it in the climax. (Do <i>not</i> read these spoilers if you have <i>not</i> read the book yet! You will destroy the experience!!) <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Rovender, one of the fist creatures Eva meets outside of Sanctuary, is the reason for the boost in my rating. Early on he briefly mentions (only once) that he used to have a family, (wife, and a few children), and that simply they were taken from him. The subject is completely forgotten, until one of the <i>very</i> last chapters. Muthr is tragically destroyed by the story's villain, leaving Eva alone with Rovender. After hours of silence, and Rovender "drinking" himself away, he begins to mutter and retort things about the feelings of losing a loved one. His sad and dismal ramblings end with him smashing a few items, and sobs of utter pain. This is an extremely realistic reaction to loss, and re-conjured pain. Rovender's sudden outburst of emotions, after appearing as a grouchy, scraggly, old man who kept mostly to himself, immediately churns up feelings of distress. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I cried, and cried. I even went back to that scene to cry some more.<br />Now that relationships have been sewn, I am so eager to continue to the next installment.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5562770694036432214" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_129186269" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/129186269" />
    <a title="Madeline Smoot" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2661354-madeline-smoot"><img alt="Madeline Smoot" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442484410p2/2661354.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/129186269?book_show_action=true">Nov 03, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Madeline Smoot" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Madeline Smoot" href="/user/show/2661354-madeline-smoot">Madeline Smoot</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2661354-madeline-smoot?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer129186269" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16149324625820928268">Eva Nine has never ventured out of her underground Sanctuary where she lives alone with her robot caretaker, Muthr. When she is finally forced out of her home by a strange sentient life form unlike anything in her Sanctuary’s database, she discovers that the world she live on is unlike the one she had expected. Instead of Earth trees and animals, she is faced with the dangerous creatures and aliens of Orbana. Hunted by one of the aliens while befriended by others, Eva sets out from her destroyed</span>
  <span id="freeText16149324625820928268" style="display:none">Eva Nine has never ventured out of her underground Sanctuary where she lives alone with her robot caretaker, Muthr. When she is finally forced out of her home by a strange sentient life form unlike anything in her Sanctuary’s database, she discovers that the world she live on is unlike the one she had expected. Instead of Earth trees and animals, she is faced with the dangerous creatures and aliens of Orbana. Hunted by one of the aliens while befriended by others, Eva sets out from her destroyed Sanctuary in an effort to find any other humans that may be left.<br /><br />This magical, and at times downright terrifying, reworking of the Wizard of Oz in a science fiction context has to be my favorite of the DiTerlizzi novels to date. Like Dorothy, Eva just wants to find her way back to a home and a family. The companions she picks up at the beginning of her journey are not the simplistic characters from Oz though, each defined by a single trait. Instead, they also grow and learn about themselves during the journey. Making this a satisfying and great story to read.<br /><br />And of course, I would be neglecting a huge portion of the book if I didn’t comment on the beautiful artwork. Admittedly, my favorite DiTerlizzi drawings will probably always be in The Spider and the Fly, but the ones in this book are amazing as well. They help bring the world to life, and they add an extra element not normally found in middle grade novels — even illustrated ones.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16149324625820928268" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_171540344" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/171540344" />
    <a title="Wolf" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4242619-wolf"><img alt="Wolf" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307369700p2/4242619.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/171540344?book_show_action=true">May 27, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wolf" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wolf" href="/user/show/4242619-wolf">Wolf</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer171540344" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6668458788708464130">This would have to be the absolute best book I have ever read, and that's saying something because I have been reading books since I was two years old. This is a wonderful, spellbinding, and creative novel written by the author of the Spiderwick Chronicles. The book takes place in the future, and it is about a 12 year old girl named Eva Nine, who has lived in an underground sanctuary her whole life, never having seen another human being, with only her protective robot guardian, M.U.T.H.R.(That s</span>
  <span id="freeText6668458788708464130" style="display:none">This would have to be the absolute best book I have ever read, and that's saying something because I have been reading books since I was two years old. This is a wonderful, spellbinding, and creative novel written by the author of the Spiderwick Chronicles. The book takes place in the future, and it is about a 12 year old girl named Eva Nine, who has lived in an underground sanctuary her whole life, never having seen another human being, with only her protective robot guardian, M.U.T.H.R.(That stands for Multi-Utility Task-Help Robot.) for companionship. Eva has a secret collection of toys and other items with which she comes to talk when she needs to be alone. The only item in this collection not given to her by M.U.T.H.R. is a battered scrap of paper depicting the image of a smiling child, adult, and robot. Eva dubbed the item "Wondla" because that is the only word intelligible on the paper. The paper is very precious to Eva, as she is positive it is the only clue she has to finding other human beings. Her life goes on in this sanctuary, somewhat monotonously, until one day a hostile intruder attacks the sanctuary, forcing Eva to flee, leaving M.U.T.H.R. behind. Once outside, she realizes that the planet she is on is not, in fact, Earth, as she thought, but instead, a planet called Orbona. During her quest to solve the many mysteries presented to her, she meets many creatures, friend and foe, discovers much, and in the end, goes on the adventure of a lifetime.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6668458788708464130" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('RA+AE+hpyNqVUQmyl3GDISFJrSpYB6j4RFwJqN4Cg3TvQqqHCc/zQY3oUoljnKreQXKUd81uHSSXtXuvfjkIQg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('RveT6kXoc68/z5zI3vny4QHa6tGIEpMt3V3AJZP+Rgnturl+pE5INCd2x/MqFNseYeHTjB17JvEOtLIiM8XNPw==')})

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer8672204035438429408">New York Times bestselling author and illustrator Tony DiTerlizzi has been creating children’s books for nearly two decades. From fanciful picture books like The Spider & The Fly (a Caldecott Honor book), to chapter books like Kenny and The Dragon and the WondLa trilogy, DiTerlizzi imbues his stories with a rich imagination. With Holly Black, he created the middle-grade series, The Spiderwick Chro</span>
  <span id="freeText8672204035438429408" style="display:none">New York Times bestselling author and illustrator Tony DiTerlizzi has been creating children’s books for nearly two decades. From fanciful picture books like The Spider &amp; The Fly (a Caldecott Honor book), to chapter books like Kenny and The Dragon and the WondLa trilogy, DiTerlizzi imbues his stories with a rich imagination. With Holly Black, he created the middle-grade series, The Spiderwick Chronicles, which has sold millions of copies, been adapted into a feature film, and has been translated in over thirty countries. He teamed up with Lucasfilm to retell the original Star Wars trilogy as a picture book and his collaboration with acclaimed author Mo Willems created the bestselling The Story of Diva &amp; Flea. The beginning of his storied career is showcased in Realms: The Roleplaying Game Art of Tony DiTerlizzi. He has been featured in Time magazine, USA Today, CNN, PBS, the BBC and The Today Show.</span>
